<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this paper, a novel carrier leakage suppression (CLS) front-end for UHF RF identification (RFID) reader is presented. We demonstrated through experiment in the laboratory environment that the proposed CLS front-end has a significant improvement in the carrier-to-data ratio by more than 36 dBc in the UHF RFID frequency band. When inserted between the antenna and a Class-1 RFID reader, measurements show that the reader can successfully demodulate the generated tag signal for a power level of -80 dBm, which corresponds to the backscattered power at 20-m distance. The read range of the reader with the proposed CLS front-end is verified again in an indoor environment. The measured read range is found to be about 23 m for a commercial battery-assisted passive (BAP) tag. We showed that a Class-3 RFID system for a long read range of 20 m can be successfully established with BAP tags and the Class-1 reader with the proposed CLS front-end.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF identification (RFID) is a promising technology that is gradually replacing the existing barcode system, which has been widely used for variety of applications, such as inventory and supply chain management. It also has lots of advantages over the barcode system when connected to internet via host computer <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. A Class-1 RFID system utilizing UHF frequency band <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a> is conventionally composed of a reader and passive tags. The reader interrogates a passive-tag attached to items by sending approximately an effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP) 4-W signal. The tag sends back the data stored in an internal memory to the reader using backscattering modulation. Backscattering modulation is formed by reflecting a received signal from the reader by altering the antenna load impedance in the passive tag according to the tag information. The reader then accesses the tag information from the backscattered signal.</p><p>A passive Class-1 tag has no internal battery and is powered up by the received signal from the reader. The reader should provide enough energy to power the tag during RF transmission. The read range of such an RFID system is chiefly determined by the received power level needed to wake-up the tag in the forward-link (reader-to-tag). The wake-up power generally becomes the tag sensitivity in a Class-1 RFID system. A typical tag sensitivity of Class-1 commercial passive tag chips ranges from â10 to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">18 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">{-}{\hbox{18 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For instance, the tag sensitivity of a Higgs-3 chip from the Alien Technology Company,<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn1" class="footnote-link"><sup>1</sup></a> which is one of the recent RFID tag chips compliant with the EPCglobal Class-1 Gen 2 protocol, is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-11" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-17"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">18 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">{-}{\hbox{18 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. With this tag sensitivity, the maximum forward-link read range is estimated to be about 12 m.</p><p>The successful application of a Class-1 RFID system stimulated the demand for a long read-range RFID system. A read range of about 20 m may be appropriate for the emerging long read-range application RFID systems, such as vehicle toll systems and the management of airline cargo containers and shipbuilding yard equipment <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. However the Class-1 passive tag generally does not have adequate sensitivity for the RFID system of 20-m read range because it is primarily determined by wake-up power. Battery-assisted passive (BAP) tags may be appropriate for such long read-range RFID systems, as it does not require wake-up power. Recently, Power ID<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn2" class="footnote-link"><sup>2</sup></a> reported a BAP tag that is compliant with the Class-1 reader. Such a BAP tag may provide an improved tag sensitivity of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-21" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">23 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">{-}{\hbox{23 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which may be used for 20-m read range. Thus, the Class-1 RFID reader with improved reader sensitivity and BAP tags may be appropriate for such long read-range RFID systems, which can be categorized as Class-3 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. The International Organization for Standardization (ISO)/International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC) has been developing standard and regulations from 2006, which were published in 2010 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>.</p><p>The Class-3 RFID system requires a reader sensitivity below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-31" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-32"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-36"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-38"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-40" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">80 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">{-}{\hbox{80 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to detect a backscattered signal at 20-m distance. However, it is very difficult to find Class-1 commercial readers with sufficient reader sensitivity to detect a tag at above 20 m due to carrier power leakage from the transmitter in a reader. For instance, the reader sensitivity of Mercury 5E from the ThingMagic Company<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn3" class="footnote-link"><sup>3</sup></a> is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-41" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-44"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-45" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-46"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-47"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-48"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-49"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-50" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">65 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">{-}{\hbox{65 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, AS3992 reader chip from Austria Microsystems is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-51" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-53"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-54"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-55" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-56"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-57"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-58"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-59"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-60" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">76 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">{-}{\hbox{76 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>,<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn4" class="footnote-link"><sup>4</sup></a> and the read range of Speedway from Impinj is limited to about 16.6 m.<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn5" class="footnote-link"><sup>5</sup></a></p><p>Conventional suppression of the carrier leakage by filters in modern mobile communications is not efficient. In mobile communications, there is sufficient bandgap between the spectra of transmitting and received signals. For example, the bandgap of above 20 MHz is allocated in a UHF global system for mobile communications (GSM). However, the spectrum of the leakage and that of the backscattered signal is very close. The difference is estimated to be about 40â640 kHz according to ISO/IEC 18000-6C. It is believed that such closely spaced signals are difficult to be filtered using filters of present technology.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> shows a typical block diagram of a reader. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, the leakage suppression is achieved by adding a 180Â° inverted signal, obtained using a variable attenuator and phase shifter. Most leakage suppression methods use the direct coupling compensation architecture in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. However, controlling the phase shifter and variable attenuator to minimize the leakage by feedback is highly complex. Precise tuning by microcontroller results in greater cancellation of the leakage up to about 70 dB in the laboratory environment <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Direct coupling compensation architecture.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Other researchers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a> use a mismatched directional coupler or branch-line coupler instead of the circulator in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> to improve the isolation between the power amplifier and low-noise amplifier. The control of the mismatch termination by feedback seems to be quite as complex as the architecture shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, and successfully demonstrated by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a> using microcontroller. The disadvantage of the mismatched directional coupler method may be the reduced received power, and the improvement of reader sensitivity is questionable although the isolation can be improved. Other methods using down-and up-conversion of the received signal have been proposed by some researchers; however, the structure becomes even more complicated <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a>.</p><p>Generally, the practical improvement of reader sensitivity may not be as much as the leakage suppression through a direct application of leakage suppression schemes. The key reason may be due to the environmental change of the leakage from the antenna, denoted as leakage 2 in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. Leakage 1 from the circulator isolation can be considered as constant; however, leakage 2 may be sensitive to environmental changes and is considered to be time varying. Leakage 2 changes can be generally caused by the carrier frequency change, the existence and movement of tagged items, and tagged material changes. Such changes significantly degrade the laboratory achieved leakage suppression in real environment. Thus, leakage cancellation scheme should be adjusted to properly track the leakage 2 caused by the environment change. However, such a controlling mechanism to track the changes is not an easy one considering simultaneous control of both phase and amplitude.</p><p>In this paper, first we investigate the effect of leakage 2 changes on the leakage suppression and we propose the novel leakage suppression front-end using the received signal alone. The transmitter signal is not used as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. Thus, the leakage suppression is expected to be less dependent on time and environmental changes. Simulation shows a leakage suppression of at least 39 dB. Connecting the leakage suppression front-end to a conventional reader, the reader can detect the backscattered signal of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-61" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-62"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-63"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-64"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-65" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-66"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-67"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-68"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">83 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">{-}{\hbox{83 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which corresponds to about 13-dB improvement of the reader sensitivity. Using the reader with the leakage suppression front-end, we also demonstrated the reader can detect a backscattered signal from a distance of above 20 m in an indoor environment.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Leakage Suppression RF Font-End Design</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Read-Range Analysis</h3><p>The read range of a passive RFID system can be calculated using Friis's formula, assuming an ideal propagation environment <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2a">[4]</a>. The received power to the tag from the reader, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-71" role="math" style="width: 3.306em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.946em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.95em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-72"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-73"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.946em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-75"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-76"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-77" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">X</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-80" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-81" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-82" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">P_{\rm RX,tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at a distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-83" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-84"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-85" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">r</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, can be given by <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-86" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block; min-width: 21.925em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; font-size: 111%; min-width: 21.925em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.285em 1017.72em 5.228em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-87"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="min-width: 21.925em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 21.925em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 17.721em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-1.739em 1017.72em 1.204em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; The reader's antenna generally uses a circular polarization and the tag antenna is assumed to have linear polarization. Thus, a 3-dB loss by polarization mismatch appears in both the reader-to-tag and tag-to-reader links.</p><p>Assuming the transmission loss <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-210" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; It can also be found that the receiving sensitivity of the reader should be below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-423" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; These values depend on the antenna gains of the reader and the tag and may vary. However, most antenna gains of the tag and reader in UHF RFID system are close to our calculation, the values being only slightly different.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Antenna Mismatch Effects</h3><p>In order to estimate leakage 2, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, we measured the reflected power for environmental changes using a commercial patch antenna. The antenna was a circularly polarized MACRO260 from MAC Technologies with 6-dBic gain. To estimate the worst case, the minimum distance was set 10 cm from the tagged materials. The return loss shows a change from 45 to 5 dB depending upon the location of the materials and antenna direction change. Thus, the number for the return loss due to the antenna mismatch from 45 to 5 dB is used as the worst case reference.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a> shows the simplified simulation schematic for the computation of the leakage power change for antenna mismatch. Antenna mismatch is represented by varying the value of resistor R2. The phase shifter and variable attenuator for the leakage cancellation is represented by PS1 and ATTEN1, respectively, and their values are set assuming a leakage power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-448" role="math" style="width: 10.994em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.913em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1009.79em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-449"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-450"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-451"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-452" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-453"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-454"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-455"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-456"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-457" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">leakage 1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-458" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-459" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-460"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-461"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-462"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-463" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">leakage 2</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-464" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">{({\hbox{leakage 1}} + {\hbox{leakage 2}})}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-465" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-466"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-467"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-468"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-469" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-470"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-471"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-472"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-473"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-474" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">70 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">{-}{\hbox{70 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the antenna return loss of 45 dB. The combined power is obtained using 180Â°-hybrid HYB1 and appears in resistor R1. Phase shifter PS1 is used to set the phase of the sampled signal using coupler COUP1 to 0Â°.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Schematic for the computation of the leakage power at receiver for changes in antenna mismatch. The isolation of the circulator and the coupling of the coupler are set to 40 and 10 dB, respectively. The antenna mismatch is implemented using resistor R2 and power combining is achieved using 180Â°-hybrid HYB1.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> shows the leakage power computed for a change in the antenna return loss from 5 to 45 dB and the phase change from 0Â° to 360Â°. The effect of the phase difference between the two signals is equivalent to the phase change of the phase shifter, and it is computed by sweeping the phase of the phase shifter. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>, the assumed leakage power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-475" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-476"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-477"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-478"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-479" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-480"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-481"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-482"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-483"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-484" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">70 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">{-}{\hbox{70 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the antenna return loss of 45 dB is observed and occurs when the two leakages have a phase difference of 180Â°. As the phase difference departs away from 180Â°, the cancellation decreases and a sharp null is formed around 180Â°. However, as the antenna mismatch increases, the reflected power from the antenna becomes larger and dominant, and the cancellation is not achieved. Thus, the total leakage power is almost entirely determined by the reflected power from the antenna. The leakage power is found to grow up to 21.5 dBm for a return loss of 5 dB, which corresponds to a 90-dB change of the leakage power. Thus, some kind of feedback to track the antenna mismatch is required. However, it is not simple and easy to implement such a feedback loop. Two separate feedback control signals are necessary, but only one error signal of the leakage power is available.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Calculated leakage power at the receiver for the antenna mismatch. In the computation, the return loss of the antenna changes from 5 to45 dB with a TX power of 30 dBm, and a circulator isolation of 40 dB at 910 MHz. The effect of phase difference between the two signals on the leakage power is implemented by sweeping the phase of phase shifter.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2c"><h3>C. RF Front-End Design</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> shows the block diagram of the proposed RF front-end for carrier leakage suppression (CLS). Input port in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> is connected to point A in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, the receiver input of the antenna. The output port is connected to point A' in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, the receiver input of the reader. The variable attenuator and phase shifter for the cancellation of carrier leakage in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> is removed. Thus, the combined signal of the leakage 1 and 2 appear at the input of the proposed CLS front-end, which makes the input signal slowly time varying due to the change of leakage 2 in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> caused by environment changes. To extract the carrier, the received signal is split and the carrier is obtained from the limiter and filter. The filter is used for harmonic elimination. The amplifier before the limiter is used to provide sufficient power to the latter. Note that the output power of the limiter is almost fixed for changes in the input power. Thus, the output power level of automatic gain control (AGC) is selected for the output power of the phase shifter to yield exactly the same as the filtered output power of the limiter. This can be realized using the AGC control input. Once set, the output powers of the two paths can be made equal without regard to the input power change. Thus, amplitude tuning for matching is not necessary, and leakage cancellation is achieved by phase tuning alone. The phase shifter is used for the cancellation of carriers by providing a phase difference of 180Â°. The carrier component is eliminated when the phase difference between the two paths becomes 180Â°. The structure is similar to that in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_2c">[21]</a>. The difference is in the employment of the AGC and phase shifter.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Proposed CLS front-end.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The operation of the proposed CLS RF front-end was simulated using Agilent ADS. First, the backscattered signal was generated using the tag emulator when it was exposed to a 910-MHz CW signal of 30 dBm. The tag emulator generates the standard Class-1 FM0 40-kb/s signal. The backscattered power was set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-485" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-486"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-487"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-488"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-489" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-490"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-491"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-492"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-493"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-494" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">80 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">{-}{\hbox{80 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> considering the power level at a 20-m distance in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>. The CW leakage carrier signal was then superimposed. The power level of the carrier leakage was set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-495" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-496"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-497"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-498"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-499" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-500"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-501"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-502"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-503"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">{-}{\hbox{10 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, assuming the transmitting power of the reader to be 30 dBm and the isolation between transmitter and receiver to be 40 dB. The synthesized signal was then converted to data using VSA 89600, which can be used as an envelope simulation source in ADS.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(a)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">(b)</a> show the spectrum of the two signals at the phase shifter output (point M1 in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>) and filter output (point M2 in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>). The spectrum of the phase shifter output includes the backscattered modulated components. The carrier leakage power is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-505" role="math" style="width: 4.868em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.387em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.39em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-506"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-507"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-508"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-509" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-510"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-511"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-512"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-513"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-514" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">7.3 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">{-}{\hbox{7.3 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the peak power level of the backscattered signal is observed to be about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-515" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-516"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-518"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-519" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-520"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-521"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-522"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-523"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-524" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">77 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">{-}{\hbox{77 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The carrier-to-data ratio is computed to be about 69 dBc.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Simulated spectra (a) at the phase shifter (point M1), (b) at the filter outputs(point M2), and (c) at the output in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>. In the simulation, the carrier leakage input power is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-525" role="math" style="width: 5.096em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.038em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1004.04em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-526"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-527"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-528"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-529" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-530"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-531"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-532"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-533"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-534" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">{-}{\hbox{10 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with AGC saturated power of 0 dBm, limiter output power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-535" role="math" style="width: 5.427em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.302em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1004.3em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-536"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-537"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-538"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-539" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-540"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-541"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-542"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-543"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-544" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">4.8 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">{-}{\hbox{4.8 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and phase shifter and filter insertion losses of 2 and 2.5 dB, respectively.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>On the contrary, the spectrum of the filter output is observed to be close to a single tone output. The backscattered signal is found to be almost disappeared, and the carrier extraction path is found to work properly. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(c)</a> shows the spectrum of the output signal. From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(c)</a>, the carrier-to-data ratio is found to be about 34 dBc, and the improvement in carrier-to-data ratio is estimated to be about 35 dB. Thus, the improvement in reader sensitivity can be expected from the improvement in carrier-to-data ratio. Also note that such improvement in the carrier-to-data ratio is obtained using the received signal alone. The leakage power level and carrier-to-data ratio are compared with those of other researchers in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a>. Although the backscattered signal is lowest due to the power level at 20 m distance, the carrier-to-data ratio is comparable to other works.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Comparison of Leakage Powers and Carrier-to-Datas Ratio<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>The input power of the proposed CLS front-end can be considered as the combined power of leakage 1 and leakage 2 in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, which is also dependent on the antenna mismatch. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a> shows the output power of the proposed CLS front-end for changes in the return loss of the antenna. The output power is observed to be almost constant. The power level of the output power is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-545" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-546"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-547"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-548"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-549" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-550"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-551"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-552"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-553"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-554" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">47 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">{-}{\hbox{47 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is the same power as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(c)</a>. To find the leakage input power change for the antenna mismatch, the simulation schematic is constructed for the same circulator isolation and antenna mismatch as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a> and the coupler, phase shifters, and variable attenuator are removed. Also the circulator port for the receiver is directly connected to resistor R1 without the the 180Â°-hybrid. The phase difference between the two signals is implemented by inserting a phase shifter between the circulator and mismatch resistor. The phase is set to 1/2 of the phase difference considering a round trip phase of the reflecting signal. The computed input power level is between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-555" role="math" style="width: 7.21em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.489em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.49em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-556"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-557"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-558"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-559" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-560"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-561"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-562"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-563"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-564" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">17</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-565" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-566" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-567"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-568"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-569"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-570" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">25 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">{- {\hbox{17}}}\sim {\hbox {25 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The maximum power level difference is due to the removal of the 180Â°-hybrid and the difference in the minimum level from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-571" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-572"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-573"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-574"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-575" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-576"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-577"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-578"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-579"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-580" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">70 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">{-}{\hbox{70 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is due to the incomplete cancellation between the two signals appearing to the port resistor R1. However, even in the case of the close cancellation reaching the minimum power level of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-581" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-582"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-583"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-584"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-585" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-586"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-587"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-588"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-589"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-590" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">70 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{-}{\hbox{70 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the result is almost the same as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Carrier leakage power at the output of the proposed CLS front-end for the antenna mismatch. The return loss of the antenna is varied from 5 to 45 dB and the circulator isolation of 40 dB.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a> shows the AGC in the simulation. The AGC is composed of a variable gain amplifier, power detecto, r and difference amplifier. The power detector AM_DemodTuned is connected to the output of the variable gain amplifier. The power detector output is compared with a reference voltage and the difference is amplified using a difference amplifier OpAmp. The output of the difference amplifier is connected to the gain control input of the variable gain amplifier. Thus, by feedback action, AGC output power yields constant output power irrespective of the input power level. When the difference amplifier gain in the feedback loop is sufficiently large, the AGC output power level is almost constant irrespective of the input power level. A constant leakage output power of the AGC is applied to the remaining block, which yields a constant leakage cancellation. Consequently the leakage output power of the proposed front-end becomes constant irrespective of the input power level, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. However, a slight change in the carrier leakage power is expected with a real AGC due to finite gain of the difference amplifier. If the change is not very significant, a constant carrier leakage power can be obtained. Therefore, the proposed CLS front-end is found to be more tolerant environmental changes than other similar studies.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>AGC simulation schematic. The power detector is implemented using narrowband power detector component AM_DemodTuned and the difference amplifier is implemented using a circuit model OpAmp in ADS.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2d"><h3>D. Implementation</h3><p>The AGC in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a> is composed of a variable gain amplifier and power detector. ADL5330 and AD 8317 from Analog Devices are selected as a variable gain amplifier and power detector, respectively. The AGC output power level is selected to yield a constant output power of 0 dBm. The output power level is set considering the power level of the filtered limiter output. Both ADL5330 and AD 8317 provide a dynamic range of 55 dB, which may not be enough for the change of the worst case leakage power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-591" role="math" style="width: 8.111em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 7.27em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1007.27em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-592"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-593"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-594"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-595" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-596"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-597"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-598"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-599"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-600" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">70</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-601" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-602" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-603"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-604"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-605"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-606" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">25.4 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">{- {\hbox{70}}}\sim {\hbox {25.4 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. However, a realistic leakage power change may be estimated between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-607" role="math" style="width: 7.21em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.489em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.49em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-608"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-609"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-610"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-611" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-612"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-613"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-614"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-615"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-616" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">20</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-617" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-618" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-619"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-620"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-621"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-622" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">{- {\hbox{20}}}\sim {\hbox {10 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which can be obtained from the simulation for the circulator isolation of 20â40 dB and antenna return loss of 20â45 dB. The simulation is similar to that for the leakage input power level for <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. The minimum leakage power level changes drastically due to cancellation in the simulation. To avoid the cancellation, the phase mismatch of 10Â° is intentionally given in the simulation.</p><p>The selected phase shifter is JSPHS-1000 from Mini Circuits, which yields an insertion loss of about 2 dB and about 200Â° phase shift at 910 MHz; however, it has a phase shift of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-623" role="math" style="width: 6.129em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.529em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.53em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-624"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-625"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.706em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1002.23em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-626"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-627"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-628" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-629" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">125</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 2.285em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-630"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-631"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-632" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-633" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â¼</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-634" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.96em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-635"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-636"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-637"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-638"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-639" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">75</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 1.024em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-640"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-641"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-642" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">{- 125}^{\circ}\sim {\hbox {75}}^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the range of which is not appropriate for leakage cancelling. To move the phase shift range, a phase delay of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-643" role="math" style="width: 3.006em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.706em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.71em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-644"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-645"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.706em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1002.23em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-646"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-647"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-648" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-649"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-650"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-651"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-652"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-653" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">120</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 2.285em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-654"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-655"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-656" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">{-{\hbox{120}}}^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 910 MHz is added. The phase filter in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a> is a filter for fixed phase delay of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-657" role="math" style="width: 3.006em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.706em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.71em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-658"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-659"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.706em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1002.23em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-660"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-661"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-663"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-664"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-665"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-666"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-667" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">120</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 2.285em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-668"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-669"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-670" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">{-{\hbox{120}}}^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 910 MHz. The phase filter is constructed using a lumped Pi-shape equivalent circuit of transmission line and is implemented using lumped chip inductors and capacitors. The implemented phase filter has an insertion loss of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-671" role="math" style="width: 2.826em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.47em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-672"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-673"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-674"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-675" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-676"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-677"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-678"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-679"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-680" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2dB</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">{-}{\hbox {2dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 910 MHz.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Block diagram of the implemented CLS front-end.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The output power of the limiter is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-681" role="math" style="width: 4.027em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.607em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.61em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-682"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-683"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-684"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-685" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-686"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-687"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-688"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-689"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-690" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">5 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">{-}{\hbox{5 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for an input power of 3â15 dBm. The Gali-52+ bamplifier from Mini Circuits is selected to supply sufficient power to the limiter. The control signal for the phase shifter is supplied by converting the digital output of the 8-bit microcontroller to analog signal. The received signal strength indicator (RSSI) block detects the leakage output power of the proposed CLS front-end. The same power detector AD8317 as in the AGC is used for the RSSI. The microcontroller receives the RSSI output signal through the 10-bit ADC in the microcontroller and is programmed to generate the appropriate control signal to minimize the output power level, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>. The leakage at the output is thus minimized. The selected components are listed in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ II</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a> shows the fabricated RF front-end for leakage suppression.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Summary of Component Specifications of the CLS Front-End<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Photograph of the fabricated CLS front-end.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Measurements</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Evaluation</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a> shows the measurement setup for the proposed CLS front-end. The TX module was set to transmit a continuous wave (CW) power level of 1 W. The tag emulator can then generate the backscattered signal at a 40â640-kHz compliant UHF RFID standard. In our experiment, tag data is established to generate FM0 40 kb/s, which is closest to the carrier frequency. The signal generated by the tag emulator is attenuated to reflect the path loss.
