</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Measurement setup of the CLS front-end.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The power level from the tag emulator was set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-691" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-692"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-693"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-694"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-695" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-696"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-697"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-698"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-699"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-700" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">80 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">{-}{\hbox{80 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which corresponds to 20-m distance. The attenuated tag signal is combined with the TX signal, which represents the leakage power of the transmitter. Note that the leakage power level to the reader emulator can also be controlled through the setup. This signal is sent to the read emulator with the proposed CLS front-end. The reader emulator has a sensitivity comparable to the conventional Class-1 reader, which can detect a tag at a distance below 10 m. There is no leakage cancellation structure in the reader emulator.</p><p>Obviously the measurement setup does not reflect the environmental changes; however, as a first step, we can find whether the leakage cancellation is successfully achieved and the reader with the proposed CLS front-end can detect the tag signal power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-701" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-702"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-703"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-704"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-705" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-706"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-707"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-708"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-709"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-710" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">80 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">{-}{\hbox{80 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> under the specified carrier leakage power level through the measurement.</p><p>The phase shift of the phase shifter in the proposed CLS front-end should be set for minimum leakage power. This can be carried out by sweeping a range of the phase tune voltage and observing the RSSI signal, which is stable for temperature change. The RSSI voltage increases as the RF input signal decreases. The phase tune voltage yielding the maximum RSSI voltage represents the minimum leakage power. The analog RSSI signal in a range of 0â2 V is converted using a 10-bit ADC in the microcontroller in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>. Of the ten bits, seven bits are allocated for the RSSI signal sampling, which allows a maximum of about 42-dB cancellation for leakage signal according to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_3a">[21]</a>. The analog control signal for the phase shifter is obtained by converting the digital signal using the 8-bit DAC in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>. However, most leakage cancellation occurs for a phase shift of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-711" role="math" style="width: 6.489em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.829em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.83em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-712"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-713"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.225em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.75em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-714"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-715"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-716" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-717"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-718"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-719"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-720"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-721" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">85</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 1.805em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-722"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-723"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-724" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-725" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â¼</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-726" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-727"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.96em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-728"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-729"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-730"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-731"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-732" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">40</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 1.024em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-733"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-734"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-735" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">{- {\hbox{85}}}^{\circ}\sim-{\hbox{40}}^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The corresponding bit number is 83â142 among the possible 256-bit numbers and the microcontroller sweeps this range of bit numbers with a step of 2 bits to reduce the sweep time. The step of 2 bit corresponds to 0.1-V phase tune voltage change. The sweep time is about 20 ms when the phase-tune voltage is altered by a 0.1-V step. This can be made shorter using fast microcontroller or increasing the step voltage. Generally, RFID readers have a dwell time of the carrier frequency set below 400 ms. Considering the dwell time, 20-ms settling time may be applicable to such an RFID system.</p><p>The starting time of the sweep for the phase tune voltage setting is determined using the lock detect (LD) signal from the reader emulator. The reader emulator synthesizes hopping frequency using a phase-locked loop (PLL) and generates a high LD signal after a lock. The microcontroller is programmed to sweep for the minimum leakage when the transition of the LD signal from low to high is found.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a> shows the measured RSSI (lower) and LD (upper) signals when the reader hops from 910, 911, 912, and 913 MHz with a 1-MHz step. From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a>, the phase tune voltage is observed to be set for the maximum RSSI, i.e., the minimum leakage after a sweep. This is found by observing the resulting RSSI signal, which is set for maximum value after the sweep.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Measured LD and RSSI waveforms for the fabricated CLS front-end using oscilloscope.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The measured spectrum of the carrier leakage to the receiver input of the reader emulator is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13</a> with and without the proposed CLS front-end. The carrier-to-data ratio, without the CLS front-end, is found to be about 73 dBc, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13(a)</a>. With the CLS front-end, the carrier-to-data ratio is observed to be about 37 dBc from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13(b)</a>, which is about a 36-dB improvement.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Measured spectra at the receiver input of the reader. (a) Without and (b) with the proposed CLS front-end. The carrier leakage power was set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-736" role="math" style="width: 5.096em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.038em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1004.04em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-737"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-738"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-739"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-740" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-741"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-742"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-743"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-744"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-745" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">{-}{\hbox{10 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the tag power of the 40-kb/s signal was set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-746" role="math" style="width: 5.096em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.038em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1004.04em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-747"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-748"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-749"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-750" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-751"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-752"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-753"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-754"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-755" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">80 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">{-}{\hbox{80 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to reflect the path loss of 20-m distance using the variable attenuators in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14</a> shows the measured output spectrum of the CLS front-end for changes in the carrier leakage power. The output power of the CLS front-end has a constant carrier leakage power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-756" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-757"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-758"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-759"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-760" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-761"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-762"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-763"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-764"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-765" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">45 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">{-}{\hbox{45 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for changes in the carrier leakage power between 0â10 dBm. This is due to the function of the AGC in the CLS front-end. The AGC maintains an almost constant output power level for the changes in the input leakage power. Thus, the improvement in the carrier-to-data ratio becomes greater for a fixed backscattered power. From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14</a>, the CLS is about 55 dB at a carrier leakage input power of 10 dBm and 45 dB at a carrier leakage input power of 0 dBm. Thus, the CLS is dependent on the carrier leakage input power and is more than 36 dB when the leakage input power is greater than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-766" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-767"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-768"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-769"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-770" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-771"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-772"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-773"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-774"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-775" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">{-}{\hbox{10 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as shown in the results of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 13</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">14</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>Measured spectra at the output of the CLS front-end for changes in the input leakage power of 0 and 10 dBm.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a> shows the demodulated baseband waveforms. The top waveform is the baseband waveform from the tag emulator, which is modulated with FM0 40 kb/s. The demodulated waveforms using the reader emulator for carrier leakage power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-776" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-777"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-778"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-779"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-780" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-781"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-782"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-783"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-784"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-785" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">{-}{\hbox{10 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and backscattered signal power of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-786" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-787"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-788"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-789"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-790" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-791"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-792"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-793"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-794"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-795" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">80 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">{-}{\hbox{80 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are also shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a>. Thus, the input carrier-to-data ratio is about 70 dBc, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13(a)</a>. The waveform in the middle is the demodulated waveform using the reader emulator without the proposed CLS front-end. The waveform has distortion compared with the original tag emulator waveform, and shows high bit error. The lower waveform is the demodulated waveform of the reader emulator with the proposed CLS front-end. The waveform is observed to faithfully track the original tag waveform. The reader can successfully obtain the tag information due to efficient CLS of more than 36 dB. Similar results were also obtained for other modulation frequencies between 40â300 kHz.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15. </b><fig><p>Baseband waveform of tag emulator (<i>top</i>), demodulated output waveforms of the reader without (<i>middle</i>) and with (<i>bottom</i>) the CLS front-end. Modulation frequency of the tag emulator is 40 kb/s.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Indoor Measurement</h3><p>Indoor measurement was carried out to validate the read range of above 20 m. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 16</a> illustrates the read-range measurement setup. The tag is attached to a plastic board, and is moved away from the reader's antenna in a 10-cm step. The read range is measured for a radiated power of 30 dBm from the reader. A commercial passive tag of an ALN-9640 chip from the Alien Technology Company and a BAP tag of a PowerG from the PowerID Company are used. The read range is determined by the maximum distance that reader can identify the tag.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16. </b><fig><p>Photograph of indoor measurement setup.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6164286/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Two commercial readers are also employed, IU9003 from LS Electronics<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn6" class="footnote-link"><sup>6</sup></a> and ALR9900 from the Alien Technology Company<a ref-type="fn" anchor="fn7" class="footnote-link"><sup>7</sup></a> for comparison. Both reader performances are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ III</a>. As tags for measurement, a commercial ALN-9640 tag from the Alien Technology Company and PowerG tag from the Power ID Company are used in the measurement. The ALN-9640 is a passive tag, while the PowerG tag is a BAP tag. Their parameters are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table4" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ IV</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table III </b>Reader Specifications<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table III" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table4"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table IV </b>RFID Tag Specifications<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-4-small.gif" alt="Table IV" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>In the measurement, the antenna for the commercial readers was replaced by a circularly polarized MACRO260 from MAC Technologies with 6-dBic gain. The IU9003 reader can detect the ALN-9640 tag and PowerG tag up to at a distance of 10 and 10.3 m, respectively. The ALR9900 reader can detect the tags up to at a distance of 9.1â9.9 m, respectively. The maximum read range is generally about 10 m, regardless of the kind of tag. Thus, the reader sensitivities of IU9003 and ALR9900 are computed to be about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-796" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-797"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-798"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-799"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-800" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-801"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-802"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-803"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-804"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-805" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">69 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">{-}{\hbox{69 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> using the plot in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>.</p><p>The read range is also measured using the reader emulator shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a>, which is compliant with EPCglobal Class-1 Gen 2 Protocol. This reader allows the connection of the proposed CLS front-end. In the case without the proposed CLS front-end, the measured read ranges approximate the two commercial readers. Thus, the sensitivity of the reader emulator without the proposed CLS front-end is estimated to be about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-806" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-807"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-808"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-809"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-810" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-811"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-812"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-813"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-814"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-815" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">69 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">{-}{\hbox{69 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Also note that the read range of the reader with the CLS front-end does not show improvement for the conventional Class-1 passive ALN-9640 tag. This is because the read range is limited by the wake-up power of the tag. However, the reader with the proposed CLS front-end has a significant improvement in read range of 23 m for the PoweG BAP tag, which corresponds to the reader sensitivity of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-816" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-817"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-818"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-819"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-820" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-821"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-822"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-823"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-824"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-825" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">84 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">{-}{\hbox{84 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> using <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>. In the case of the BAP tag, the major limitation to the read range is not in the wake-up power, but in the reader sensitivity. Thus, the reader with improved sensitivity can detect tag in a long read range. The results of the read range are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table5" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ V</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table5"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table V </b>Results of Read Range<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-5-small.gif" alt="Table V" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>Using the measured read ranges in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table5" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ V</a>, the sensitivities are computed and summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table6" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ VI</a>. In <a ref-type="table" anchor="table6" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ VI</a>, the sensitivities of the readers from other researchers are also compared. From <a ref-type="table" anchor="table6" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ VI</a>, it can be found that the proposed leakage suppression font-end improves the reader sensitivity by about 13 dB. The reader with the proposed leakage suppression front-end also shows an excellent reader sensitivity. This implies that a successful Class-3 RFID system for a long read range can be constructed with the Class-1 reader with the proposed CLS front-end and BAP tags.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table6"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table VI </b>Reader Sensitivities<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6191380/6164286/6164286-table-6-small.gif" alt="Table VI" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>We have proposed a novel CLS front-end based on the received signal alone. The leakage suppression is thus less dependent on time and environmental changes. We demonstrated experimentally that the proposed CLS front-end provides a significant improvement in the carrier-to-data ratio by up to more than 36 dBc, which is consistent with our simulation results. We also demonstrated through indoor experiment that the reader with the proposed CLS front-end can detect a commercial Class-1 battery-assisted tag at a distance of above 20 m. We believe that the proposed CLS front-end if installed in the Class-1 reader will be applicable to long read-range RFID systems requiring about 20-m distance.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
